<p></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Plot">Plot</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=1" title="Edit section: Plot">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>Dominick "Dom" Cobb (<a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>) and Arthur (<a href="/wiki/Joseph_Gordon-Levitt" title="Joseph Gordon-Levitt">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a>) are "extractors", people who perform <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Corporate_espionage" title="Corporate espionage">corporate espionage</a> using an experimental military technology to infiltrate the <a href="/wiki/Unconscious_mind" title="Unconscious mind">subconscious</a> of their targets and extract information while experiencing <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shared_dreaming" title="Shared dreaming">shared dreaming</a>. Their latest target is Japanese businessman Saito (<a href="/wiki/Ken_Watanabe" title="Ken Watanabe">Ken Watanabe</a>). The extraction from Saito fails when sabotaged by a memory of Cobb's deceased wife Mal (<a href="/wiki/Marion_Cotillard" title="Marion Cotillard">Marion Cotillard</a>). Saito reveals that he was actually auditioning the team to perform the difficult act of "inception": planting an idea in a person's subconscious.</p>
<p>In order to break up the <a href="/wiki/Energy_industry" title="Energy industry">energy</a> <a href="/wiki/Conglomerate_(company)" title="Conglomerate (company)">conglomerate</a> of ailing competitor Maurice Fischer (<a href="/wiki/Pete_Postlethwaite" title="Pete Postlethwaite">Pete Postlethwaite</a>), Saito wants Cobb to plant into the mind of Fischer's son and heir, Robert (<a href="/wiki/Cillian_Murphy" title="Cillian Murphy">Cillian Murphy</a>), the idea of dissolving his father's company. Should Cobb succeed, Saito tells Cobb he will use his influence to clear Cobb of a murder charge, which will allow Cobb to return home to his children. Although Arthur claims that inception is impossible as it is always possible to trace the origin of an idea, Cobb, claiming past experience, accepts the offer and sets about assembling his team: Eames (<a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a>), a conman and identity forger; Yusuf (<a href="/wiki/Dileep_Rao" title="Dileep Rao">Dileep Rao</a>), a chemist who concocts a powerful <a href="/wiki/Sedative" title="Sedative">sedative</a> for a stable "<a href="/wiki/False_awakening" title="False awakening">dream within a dream</a>" strategy; Ariadne (<a href="/wiki/Ellen_Page" title="Ellen Page">Ellen Page</a>), an architecture student tasked with designing the <a href="/wiki/Labyrinth" title="Labyrinth">labyrinth</a> of the dream landscapes, recruited with the help of Professor Stephen Miles (<a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a>). Saito insists on accompanying the team to verify their success. When Ariadne shares a dream with Cobb, he reveals to her that his subconscious recreates Mal, and she appears frequently in his dreams as a hostile force.</p>
<p>When the elder Fischer dies in Sydney, Robert Fischer accompanies the body on a flight back to Los Angeles, which the team uses as an opportunity to isolate Fischer. Cobb sedates him, bringing him into a shared dream with the extractors. At each level in the layered dreaming, the person generating the dream stays behind to set up a "<a href="/wiki/Hypnic_jerk" title="Hypnic jerk">kick</a>" that will be used to awaken the other sleeping team members who have entered another dream layer deeper. While death in a dream would, under normal circumstances, cause the dreamer to wake up, the sedatives used to stabilize the dreams would not allow that. Thus, death during the mission will result in entering <a href="/wiki/Limbo" title="Limbo">Limbo</a>, an expanse of infinite raw subconscious from which it is very difficult to escape.</p>
<p>In the first level, the team enter Yusuf's dream of a rainy Los Angeles. The team abducts Fischer, but it emerges that Fischer has been trained to resist extraction. He reflexively creates a team of bodyguards who protect him, wounding Saito severely. Even worse, a barreling freight train plows down the avenue, batting aside cars and trucks and cutting off Cobb, Yusuf and Ariadne from the rest of the team. Eames temporarily takes the appearance of Fischer's godfather, Peter Browning (<a href="/wiki/Tom_Berenger" title="Tom Berenger">Tom Berenger</a>), to suggest Fischer reconsider his father's <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Will_(law)" title="Will (law)">will</a>. Yusuf drives the team in a van as the rest are sedated into the second level, a hotel dreamed by Arthur. On this level, the extractors recruit Fischer, convincing him that his kidnapping was orchestrated by Browning and that they are Fischer's subconscious protectors. They persuade him to go down another level to explore Browning's subconscious (whereas it is actually a ruse to enter his own). The third level is a snowy mountain fortress dreamed by Eames. Meanwhile, Yusuf, under assault in the first level, accidentally initiates his kick too soon by driving off a bridge, removing the gravity of Arthur's dream world and causing an avalanche in Eames' dream. Arthur is forced to improvise a new kick using an elevator that will be synchronized with the van hitting the water, while the team in Eames' dream races to finish the job before the new round of kicks.</p>
<p>Saito succumbs to his wounds, and Cobb's projection of Mal sabotages the plan by killing Fischer, sending them both into Limbo.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-13"><a href="#cite_note-13"><span>[</span>13<span>]</span></a></sup> Cobb and Ariadne enter Limbo to find Fischer and Saito, while Eames remains on his dream level to set up a kick by rigging the fortress with explosives. Cobb reveals to Ariadne that he and Mal went to Limbo while experimenting with the dream-sharing technology, where they spent "fifty years" of experienced time constructing a world from their shared memories while seemingly growing old together. Cobb confesses that in order to ensure Mal would leave Limbo, he had implanted the idea her reality was false in her head in the first place; this was how he knew that inception was possible. The experience destabilised Mal, and left her convinced that she was still dreaming. In an attempt to 'wake up', Mal committed suicide, and tried desperately to persuade Cobb to do so too by incriminating him in her death. Facing a murder charge, Cobb fled the U.S. His children, who appear frequently in his dreams, are in California in the care of Professor Miles, who is Mal's father.</p>
<p>Through his confession, Cobb attains <a href="/wiki/Catharsis" title="Catharsis">catharsis</a> and chooses to remain in Limbo to search for Saito. Ariadne pushes Fischer off a balcony, resuscitating him at the mountain fortress, where he enters a safe room to discover and accept the planted idea: a vision of his father telling him to be his own man, and split up his father's company. All team members other than Cobb and Saito ride the synchronized kicks back to reality: Ariadne jumps off a balcony in Limbo, Eames detonates the explosives in the fortress, Arthur blasts an elevator containing the team's sleeping bodies up an elevator shaft, and the van in Yusuf's dream hits the water. Cobb eventually finds an aged Saito in Limbo (shown <i><a href="/wiki/In_medias_res" title="In medias res">in medias res</a></i> at the start of the film) and the two remember their arrangement, presumably shooting themselves and waking to outer-world reality back on the airplane, where the entire team and Robert Fischer have awakened.</p>
<p>Upon arriving in Los Angeles, Cobb successfully passes through <a href="/wiki/U.S._Customs_and_Border_Protection" title="U.S. Customs and Border Protection">U.S. customs</a> to join his waiting father-in-law, who brings him to his children. Cobb spins a top – a totem, which will determine if he is dreaming or awake – but decides to ignore the outcome and greets his family.</p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cast">Cast</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=2" title="Edit section: Cast">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg"><img alt="A man in a black suit, a woman in a pink dress, a man in a plaid suit, a woman in a black dress, a Japanese man in a black suit, and an old man in a blue suit clap their hands, while a man in a black suit stands. A microphone stand is in the foreground, and blue curtains are in the background." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="546" data-file-width="1004" height="120" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/220px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/330px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/43/InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg/440px-InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:InceptionCastPremiereJuly10.jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
The cast at a premiere for the film in July 2010: From left to right: Cillian Murphy, Marion Cotillard, Joseph Gordon-Levitt, Ellen Page, Ken Watanabe, Michael Caine, and Leonardo DiCaprio</div>
</div>
</div>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a> as Dom Cobb, a professional thief who specializes in <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Con_artist" title="Con artist">conning</a> secrets from his victims by infiltrating their dreams. DiCaprio was the first actor to be cast in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weintraub_14-0"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan had been trying to work with the actor for years and met him several times, but was unable to convince him to appear in any of his films until <i>Inception</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threecircle_15-0"><a href="#cite_note-threecircle-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Both <a href="/wiki/Brad_Pitt" title="Brad Pitt">Brad Pitt</a> and <a href="/wiki/Will_Smith" title="Will Smith">Will Smith</a> were offered the role, according to <i><a href="/wiki/The_Hollywood_Reporter" title="The Hollywood Reporter">The Hollywood Reporter</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-16"><a href="#cite_note-16"><span>[</span>16<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Joseph_Gordon-Levitt" title="Joseph Gordon-Levitt">Joseph Gordon-Levitt</a> as Arthur, Cobb's partner who manages and researches the missions. Gordon-Levitt compared Arthur to the producer of Cobb's art, "the one saying, 'Okay, you have your vision; now I'm going to figure out how to make all the nuts and bolts work so you can do your thing'".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-17"><a href="#cite_note-17"><span>[</span>17<span>]</span></a></sup> The actor did all of his stunts but one scene and said the preparation "was a challenge and it would have to be for it to look real".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-18"><a href="#cite_note-18"><span>[</span>18<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/James_Franco" title="James Franco">James Franco</a> was in talks with Christopher Nolan to play Arthur, but was ultimately unavailable due to scheduling conflicts.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ellen_Page" title="Ellen Page">Ellen Page</a> as Ariadne, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Graduate_student" title="Graduate student">graduate student</a> of <a href="/wiki/Architecture" title="Architecture">architecture</a> who is recruited to construct the various dreamscapes, which are described as mazes. The name <a href="/wiki/Ariadne" title="Ariadne">Ariadne</a> alludes to a princess of <a href="/wiki/Greek_mythology" title="Greek mythology">Greek myth</a>, daughter of <a href="/wiki/Minos" title="Minos">King Minos</a>, who aided the hero <a href="/wiki/Theseus" title="Theseus">Theseus</a> by giving him a sword and a ball of string to help him navigate the labyrinth which was the prison of the <a href="/wiki/Minotaur" title="Minotaur">Minotaur</a>. Nolan said that Page was chosen for being a "perfect combination of freshness and savvy and maturity beyond her years".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-19"><a href="#cite_note-19"><span>[</span>19<span>]</span></a></sup> Page said her character acts as a proxy to the audience, as "she's just learning about these ideas and, in essence, assists the audience in learning about dream sharing".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-20"><a href="#cite_note-20"><span>[</span>20<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Evan_Rachel_Wood" title="Evan Rachel Wood">Evan Rachel Wood</a> was Christopher Nolan's first choice to play Ariadne, but she turned it down. Before Ellen Page was offered and accepted the role, Nolan considered casting <a href="/wiki/Emily_Blunt" title="Emily Blunt">Emily Blunt</a>, <a href="/wiki/Rachel_McAdams" title="Rachel McAdams">Rachel McAdams</a>, <a href="/wiki/Taylor_Swift" title="Taylor Swift">Taylor Swift</a>, <a href="/wiki/Emma_Roberts" title="Emma Roberts">Emma Roberts</a>, <a href="/wiki/Jessy_Schram" title="Jessy Schram">Jessy Schram</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Carey_Mulligan" title="Carey Mulligan">Carey Mulligan</a>.<sup class="noprint Inline-Template Template-Fact" style="white-space:nowrap;">[<i><a href="/wiki/Wikipedia:Citation_needed" title="Wikipedia:Citation needed"><span title="This claim needs references to reliable sources. (January 2015)">citation needed</span></a></i>]</sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Hardy" title="Tom Hardy">Tom Hardy</a> as Eames, a sharp-tongued associate of Cobb's. He is referred to as a <a href="/wiki/Fence_(criminal)" title="Fence (criminal)">fence</a> but his specialty is <a href="/wiki/Forgery" title="Forgery">forgery</a>, more accurately <a href="/wiki/Identity_theft" title="Identity theft">identity theft</a>. Eames uses his ability to <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Impersonation" title="Impersonation">impersonate others</a> inside the dream world in order to manipulate Fischer. Hardy described his character as "an old, <a href="/wiki/Graham_Greene" title="Graham Greene">Graham Greene</a>-type diplomat; sort of faded, shabby, grandeur – the old Shakespeare lovey mixed with somebody from <a href="/wiki/United_Kingdom_Special_Forces" title="United Kingdom Special Forces">Her Majesty's Special Forces</a>", who wears "campy, old money" costumes.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-21"><a href="#cite_note-21"><span>[</span>21<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Ken_Watanabe" title="Ken Watanabe">Ken Watanabe</a> as Mr. Saito, a Japanese businessman who employs Cobb for the team's mission. Nolan wrote the role with Watanabe in mind, as he wanted to work with him again after <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pn10_22-0"><a href="#cite_note-pn10-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Inception</i> is Watanabe's first work in a contemporary setting where his primary language is English. Watanabe tried to emphasize a different characteristic of Saito in every dream level – "First chapter in my castle, I pick up some hidden feelings of the cycle. It's magical, powerful and then the first dream. And back to the second chapter, in the old hotel, I pick up [being] sharp and more calm and smart and it's a little bit [of a] different process to make up the character of any movie".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-23"><a href="#cite_note-23"><span>[</span>23<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Dileep_Rao" title="Dileep Rao">Dileep Rao</a> as Yusuf. Rao describes Yusuf as "an avant-garde pharmacologist, who is a resource for people, like Cobb, who want to do this work unsupervised, unregistered and unapproved of by anyone". Co-producer Jordan Goldberg said the role of the chemist was "particularly tough because you don't want him to seem like some kind of drug dealer", and that Rao was cast for being "funny, interesting and obviously smart".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._11_24-0"><a href="#cite_note-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._11-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Cillian_Murphy" title="Cillian Murphy">Cillian Murphy</a> as Robert Michael Fischer, the heir to a business empire and the team's target.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pn10_22-1"><a href="#cite_note-pn10-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup> Murphy said Fischer was portrayed as "a petulant child who's in need of a lot of attention from his father, he has everything he could ever want materially, but he's deeply lacking emotionally". The actor also researched the sons of <a href="/wiki/Rupert_Murdoch" title="Rupert Murdoch">Rupert Murdoch</a>, "to add to that the idea of living in the shadow of someone so immensely powerful".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-25"><a href="#cite_note-25"><span>[</span>25<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Tom_Berenger" title="Tom Berenger">Tom Berenger</a> as Peter Browning, Robert Fischer's <a href="/wiki/Godparent" title="Godparent">godfather</a> and fellow executive at the Fischers' company.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CinemaRewind_26-0"><a href="#cite_note-CinemaRewind-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> Berenger said Browning acts as a "surrogate father" to Robert, who calls the character "Uncle Peter", and emphasized that "Browning has been with [Robert] his whole life and has probably spent more quality time with him than his own father".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._11_24-1"><a href="#cite_note-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._11-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Marion_Cotillard" title="Marion Cotillard">Marion Cotillard</a> as Mal Cobb, Dom's deceased wife. She is a manifestation of Dom's guilt about the real cause of Mal's suicide. He is unable to control these projections of her, challenging his abilities as an extractor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threecircle_15-1"><a href="#cite_note-threecircle-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan described Mal as "the essence of the <a href="/wiki/Femme_fatale" title="Femme fatale">femme fatale</a>," and DiCaprio praised Cotillard's performance saying that "she can be strong and vulnerable and hopeful and heartbreaking all in the same moment, which was perfect for all the contradictions of her character".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-27"><a href="#cite_note-27"><span>[</span>27<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Pete_Postlethwaite" title="Pete Postlethwaite">Pete Postlethwaite</a> as Maurice Fischer, Robert Fischer's father and the dying founder of a business empire. The film became the first of Postlethwaite's final three film roles before his death in early 2011.</li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a> as Professor Stephen Miles, Cobb's mentor and father-in-law,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._11_24-2"><a href="#cite_note-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._11-24"><span>[</span>24<span>]</span></a></sup> and Ariadne's college professor who recommends her to the team.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InContention_28-0"><a href="#cite_note-InContention-28"><span>[</span>28<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Lukas_Haas" title="Lukas Haas">Lukas Haas</a> as Nash, an architect in Cobb's employment who betrays the team and is later replaced by Ariadne.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-29"><a href="#cite_note-29"><span>[</span>29<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<ul>
<li><a href="/wiki/Talulah_Riley" title="Talulah Riley">Talulah Riley</a> as a woman whom Eames disguises himself as in a dream. Riley liked the role, despite it being minimal – "I get to wear a nice dress, pick up men in bars, and shove them in elevators. It was good to do something adultish. Usually I play 15-year-old English schoolgirls."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-30"><a href="#cite_note-30"><span>[</span>30<span>]</span></a></sup></li>
</ul>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Production">Production</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=3" title="Edit section: Production">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Development">Development</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=4" title="Edit section: Development">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tleft">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="2048" data-file-width="3648" height="124" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG/220px-Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG/330px-Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/3e/Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG/440px-Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Emma_Thomas_%26_Christopher_Nolan_at_WonderCon_2010_1.JPG" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Emma Thomas and Christopher Nolan answer questions about <i>Inception</i>. The husband and wife team produced the film through their company <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Syncopy_Films" title="Syncopy Films">Syncopy Films</a>. Nolan also wrote and directed it.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Initially, Nolan wrote an 80-page <a href="/wiki/Film_treatment" title="Film treatment">treatment</a> about dream-stealers.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_5-1"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> Originally, Nolan had envisioned <i>Inception</i> as a <a href="/wiki/Horror_film" title="Horror film">horror film</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_5-2"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> but eventually wrote it as a <a href="/wiki/Heist_film" title="Heist film">heist film</a> even though he found that "traditionally [they] are very deliberately superficial in emotional terms."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_31-0"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Upon revisiting his script, he decided that basing it in that genre did not work because the story "relies so heavily on the idea of the interior state, the idea of dream and <a href="/wiki/Memory" title="Memory">memory</a>. I realized I needed to raise the emotional stakes."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_31-1"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan worked on the script for nine to ten years.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weintraub_14-1"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> When he first started thinking about making the film, Nolan was influenced by "that era of movies where you had <i><a href="/wiki/The_Matrix" title="The Matrix">The Matrix</a></i> (1999), you had <i><a href="/wiki/Dark_City_(1998_film)" title="Dark City (1998 film)">Dark City</a></i> (1998), you had <i><a href="/wiki/The_Thirteenth_Floor" title="The Thirteenth Floor">The Thirteenth Floor</a></i> (1999) and, to a certain extent, you had <i><a href="/wiki/Memento_(film)" title="Memento (film)">Memento</a></i> (2000), too. They were based in the principles that the world around you might not be real."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_31-2"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-32"><a href="#cite_note-32"><span>[</span>32<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Nolan first pitched the film to Warner Bros. in 2001, but then felt that he needed more experience making large-scale films, and embarked on <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzkoff_6-1"><a href="#cite_note-Itzkoff-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> He soon realized that a film like <i>Inception</i> needed a large budget because "as soon as you're talking about dreams, the potential of the human mind is infinite. And so the scale of the film has to feel infinite. It has to feel like you could go anywhere by the end of the film. And it has to work on a massive scale."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzkoff_6-2"><a href="#cite_note-Itzkoff-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> After making <i>The Dark Knight</i>, Nolan decided to make <i>Inception</i> and spent six months completing the script.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzkoff_6-3"><a href="#cite_note-Itzkoff-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan states that the key to completing the script was wondering what would happen if several people shared the same dream. "Once you remove the privacy, you've created an infinite number of alternative universes in which people can meaningfully interact, with validity, with weight, with dramatic consequences."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzkoff2_33-0"><a href="#cite_note-Itzkoff2-33"><span>[</span>33<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Leonardo DiCaprio was the first actor to be cast in the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weintraub_14-2"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan had been trying to work with the actor for years and met him several times, but was unable to convince him to appear in any of his films until <i>Inception</i>. DiCaprio finally agreed because he was "intrigued by this concept—this dream-heist notion and how this character's going to unlock his dreamworld and ultimately affect his real life."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jolin_34-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jolin-34"><span>[</span>34<span>]</span></a></sup> He read the script and found it to be "very well written, comprehensive but you really had to have Chris in person, to try to articulate some of the things that have been swirling around his head for the last eight years."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Itzkoff_6-4"><a href="#cite_note-Itzkoff-6"><span>[</span>6<span>]</span></a></sup> DiCaprio and Nolan spent months talking about the screenplay. Nolan took a long time re-writing the script in order "to make sure that the emotional journey of his character was the driving force of the movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weintraub_14-3"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> On February 11, 2009, it was announced that <a href="/wiki/Warner_Bros." title="Warner Bros.">Warner Bros.</a> purchased <i>Inception</i>, a <a href="/wiki/Spec_script" title="Spec script">spec script</a> written by Nolan.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-first_7-1"><a href="#cite_note-first-7"><span>[</span>7<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Locations_and_sets">Locations and sets <span id="Filming"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=5" title="Edit section: Locations and sets">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><a href="/wiki/Principal_photography" title="Principal photography">Principal photography</a> began in Tokyo on June 19, 2009, with the scene where Saito first hires Cobb during a helicopter flight over the city.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_5-3"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes7_35-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes7-35"><span>[</span>35<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The production moved to the United Kingdom and shot in a converted <a href="/wiki/Airship_hangar" title="Airship hangar">airship hangar</a> in <a href="/wiki/Cardington,_Bedfordshire" title="Cardington, Bedfordshire">Cardington</a>, Bedfordshire, north of London.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes8_36-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes8-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> There, the hotel bar set which tilted 30 degrees was built.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heuring_37-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heuring-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> A hotel corridor was also constructed by <a href="/wiki/Guy_Hendrix_Dyas" title="Guy Hendrix Dyas">Guy Hendrix Dyas</a>, the production designer, <a href="/wiki/Chris_Corbould" title="Chris Corbould">Chris Corbould</a>, the special effects supervisor, and <a href="/wiki/Wally_Pfister" title="Wally Pfister">Wally Pfister</a>, the director of photography; it rotated a full 360 degrees to create the effect of alternate directions of <a href="/wiki/Gravity" title="Gravity">gravity</a> for scenes set during the second level of dreaming, where dream-sector physics become chaotic. The idea was inspired by a technique used in <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/2001:_A_Space_Odyssey_(film)" title="2001: A Space Odyssey (film)">2001: A Space Odyssey</a></i> (1968). Nolan said, "I was interested in taking those ideas, techniques, and philosophies and applying them to an action scenario".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heuring2_38-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heuring2-38"><span>[</span>38<span>]</span></a></sup> The filmmakers originally planned to make the hallway only 40 ft (12 m) long, but as the action sequence became more elaborate, the hallway's length grew to 100 ft (30 m). The corridor was suspended along eight large concentric rings that were spaced equidistantly outside its walls and powered by two massive electric motors.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes8_36-1"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes8-36"><span>[</span>36<span>]</span></a></sup> Joseph Gordon-Levitt, who plays Arthur, spent several weeks learning to fight in a corridor that spun like "a giant <a href="/wiki/Hamster_wheel" title="Hamster wheel">hamster wheel</a>".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_31-3"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan said of the device, "It was like some incredible torture device; we thrashed Joseph for weeks, but in the end we looked at the footage, and it looks unlike anything any of us has seen before. The rhythm of it is unique, and when you watch it, even if you know how it was done, it confuses your perceptions. It's unsettling in a wonderful way".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_31-4"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup> Gordon-Levitt remembered, "it was six-day weeks of just, like, coming home at night battered ... The light fixtures on the ceiling are coming around on the floor, and you have to choose the right time to cross through them, and if you don't, you're going to fall."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-39"><a href="#cite_note-39"><span>[</span>39<span>]</span></a></sup> On July 15, 2009, filming took place at <a href="/wiki/University_College_London" title="University College London">University College London</a> for the sequences occurring inside a Paris college of architecture in the story,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_5-4"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> including the library, Flaxman Gallery and Gustav Tuck Theatre.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-40"><a href="#cite_note-40"><span>[</span>40<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Filming moved to France where they shot Cobb entering the college of architecture (the place used for the entrance was the <a href="/wiki/Mus%C3%A9e_Galliera" title="Musée Galliera">Musée Galliera</a>) and the pivotal scenes between Ariadne and Cobb, in a <a href="/wiki/Bistro" title="Bistro">bistro</a> (a fictional one set up at the corner of Rue César Franck and Rue Bouchut) and then on the <a href="/wiki/Pont_de_Bir-Hakeim" title="Pont de Bir-Hakeim">Bir-Hakeim bridge</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes9_41-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes9-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup> For the explosion that takes place during the bistro scene, the local authorities would not allow the actual use of explosives. High-pressure <a href="/wiki/Nitrogen" title="Nitrogen">nitrogen</a> was used to create the effect of a series of explosions. Pfister used six high-speed cameras to capture the sequence from different angles and make sure that they got the shot. The visual effects department then enhanced the sequence, adding more destruction and flying debris. For the "Paris folding" sequence and when Ariadne "creates" the bridges, green screen and CGI were used on location.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes9_41-1"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes9-41"><span>[</span>41<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Tangier" title="Tangier">Tangier</a>, Morocco, doubled as <a href="/wiki/Mombasa" title="Mombasa">Mombasa</a>, where Cobb hires Eames and Yusuf. A foot chase was shot in the streets and alleyways of the historic <a href="/wiki/Medina_quarter" title="Medina quarter">medina quarter</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes10_42-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes10-42"><span>[</span>42<span>]</span></a></sup> To capture this sequence, Pfister employed a mix of <a href="/wiki/Hand-held_camera" title="Hand-held camera">hand-held camera</a> and <a href="/wiki/Steadicam" title="Steadicam">steadicam</a> work.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes11_43-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes11-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> Tangier was also used to film an important riot scene during the initial foray into Saito's mind.</p>
<p>Filming moved to the Los Angeles area, where some sets were built on a Warner Brothers <a href="/wiki/Sound_stage" title="Sound stage">sound stage</a>, including the interior rooms of Saito's Japanese castle (the exterior was done on a small set built in Malibu beach). The dining room was inspired by the <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Nijo_Castle" title="Nijo Castle">Nijo Castle</a> built around 1603. These sets were inspired by a mix of <a href="/wiki/Japanese_architecture" title="Japanese architecture">Japanese architecture</a> and Western influences.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes11_43-1"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes11-43"><span>[</span>43<span>]</span></a></sup> The production also staged a multi-vehicle <a href="/wiki/Car_chase" title="Car chase">car chase</a> on the streets of <a href="/wiki/Downtown_Los_Angeles" title="Downtown Los Angeles">downtown Los Angeles</a>, which involved a freight train crashing down the middle of a street.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes12_44-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes12-44"><span>[</span>44<span>]</span></a></sup> To do this, the filmmakers configured a train engine on the chassis of a tractor trailer. The replica was made from <a href="/wiki/Fiberglass" title="Fiberglass">fiberglass</a> molds taken from authentic train parts and then matched in terms of color and design.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes13_45-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes13-45"><span>[</span>45<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, the car chase was supposed to be set in the midst of a downpour but the L.A. weather stayed typically sunny. The filmmakers were forced to set up elaborate effects (e.g., rooftop <a href="/wiki/Water_cannon" title="Water cannon">water cannons</a>) to give the audience the impression that the weather was overcast and soggy. L.A. was also the site of the climactic scene where a <a href="/wiki/Ford_E-Series" title="Ford E-Series">Ford Econoline</a> van flies off the <a href="/wiki/Commodore_Schuyler_F._Heim_Bridge" title="Commodore Schuyler F. Heim Bridge">Schuyler Heim Bridge</a> in slow motion.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ditzian_46-0"><a href="#cite_note-Ditzian-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> This sequence was filmed on and off for months with the van being shot out of a cannon, according to actor Dileep Rao. Capturing the actors suspended within the van in slow motion took a whole day to film. Once the van landed in the water, the challenge for the actors was not to panic. "And when they ask you to act, it's a bit of an ask," explained Cillian Murphy.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ditzian_46-1"><a href="#cite_note-Ditzian-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> The actors had to be underwater for four to five minutes while drawing air from <a href="/wiki/Diving_cylinder" title="Diving cylinder">scuba tanks</a>; underwater <a href="/wiki/Buddy_breathing" title="Buddy breathing">buddy breathing</a> is shown in this sequence.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Ditzian_46-2"><a href="#cite_note-Ditzian-46"><span>[</span>46<span>]</span></a></sup> Cobb's house was in Pasadena. The hotel lobby was filmed at the CAA building in Century City. Limbo was made on location in Los Angeles and Morocco with the beach scene filmed at Palos Verdes beach with CGI buildings. N Hope St. in Los Angeles was the primary filming location for Limbo, with green screen and CGI being used to create the dream landscape.</p>
<p>The final phase of principal photography took place in <a href="/wiki/Alberta" title="Alberta">Alberta</a> in late November 2009. The location manager discovered a temporarily closed ski resort, <a href="/wiki/Fortress_Mountain_Resort" title="Fortress Mountain Resort">Fortress Mountain</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes14_47-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes14-47"><span>[</span>47<span>]</span></a></sup> An elaborate set was assembled near the top station of the Canadian <a href="/wiki/Chairlift" title="Chairlift">chairlift</a>, taking three months to build.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jolin2_48-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jolin2-48"><span>[</span>48<span>]</span></a></sup> The production had to wait for a huge snowstorm, which eventually arrived.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_5-5"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup> The ski-chase sequence was inspired by Nolan's favorite <a href="/wiki/James_Bond" title="James Bond">James Bond</a> film, <i><a href="/wiki/On_Her_Majesty%27s_Secret_Service_(film)" title="On Her Majesty's Secret Service (film)">On Her Majesty's Secret Service</a></i> (1969): "What I liked about it that we've tried to emulate in this film is there's a tremendous balance in that movie of action and scale and romanticism and tragedy and emotion."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Jolin3_49-0"><a href="#cite_note-Jolin3-49"><span>[</span>49<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinematography">Cinematography</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=6" title="Edit section: Cinematography">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film was shot primarily in the <a href="/wiki/Anamorphic_format" title="Anamorphic format">anamorphic format</a> on <a href="/wiki/35_mm_film" title="35 mm film">35 mm film</a>, with key sequences filmed on <a href="/wiki/70_mm_film" title="70 mm film">65 mm</a>, and aerial sequences in <a href="/wiki/VistaVision" title="VistaVision">VistaVision</a>. Nolan did not shoot any footage with <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> cameras as he had with <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i>. "We didn't feel that we were going to be able to shoot in IMAX because of the size of the cameras because this film given that it deals with a potentially surreal area, the nature of dreams and so forth, I wanted it to be as realistic as possible. Not be bound by the scale of those IMAX cameras, even though I love the format dearly".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weintraub_14-4"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> In addition Nolan and Pfister tested using <a href="/wiki/Showscan" title="Showscan">Showscan</a> and <a href="/wiki/List_of_film_formats" title="List of film formats">Super Dimension 70</a> as potential large format <a href="/wiki/High_frame_rate" title="High frame rate">high frame rate</a> camera systems to use for the film, but ultimately decided against either format.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heuring_37-1"><a href="#cite_note-Heuring-37"><span>[</span>37<span>]</span></a></sup> Sequences in slow motion were filmed on a Photo-Sonics 35mm camera at speeds of up to 1000 frames per second. Wally Pfister tested shooting some of these sequences using a high speed <a href="/wiki/Digital_cinematography" title="Digital cinematography">digital camera</a>, but found the format to be too unreliable due to technical glitches. "Out of six times that we shot on the digital format, we only had one useable piece and it didn't end up in the film. Out of the six times we shot with the Photo-Sonics camera and 35mm running through it, every single shot was in the movie."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kodak_50-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kodak-50"><span>[</span>50<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan also chose not to shoot any of the film in <a href="/wiki/3D_film" title="3D film">3D</a> as he prefers shooting on film<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weintraub_14-5"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> using <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Prime_Lens" title="Prime Lens">prime lenses</a>, which is not possible with 3D cameras.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Playlist_51-0"><a href="#cite_note-Playlist-51"><span>[</span>51<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan has also criticised the dim image that 3D projection produces, and disputes that traditional film does not allow realistic <a href="/wiki/Depth_perception" title="Depth perception">depth perception</a>, saying "I think it's a misnomer to call it 3D versus 2D. The whole point of cinematic imagery is it's three dimensional... You know 95% of our <a href="/wiki/Depth_perception" title="Depth perception">depth cues</a> come from <a href="/wiki/Ambient_occlusion" title="Ambient occlusion">occlusion</a>, resolution, color and so forth, so the idea of calling a 2D movie a '2D movie' is a little misleading."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes-hcff_52-0"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-hcff-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan did test converting <i>Inception</i> into 3D in post-production but decided that, while it was possible, he lacked the time to complete the conversion to a standard he was happy with.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_5-6"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-latimes-hcff_52-1"><a href="#cite_note-latimes-hcff-52"><span>[</span>52<span>]</span></a></sup> In February 2011 <a href="/wiki/Jonathan_Liebesman" title="Jonathan Liebesman">Jonathan Liebesman</a> suggested that Warner Bros were attempting a 3D conversion for <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a> release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-53"><a href="#cite_note-53"><span>[</span>53<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Wally Pfister gave each location and dream level a distinctive look to aid the audience's recognition of the narrative's location during the heavily crosscut portion of the film: the mountain fortress appears sterile and cool, the hotel hallways have warm hues, and the scenes in the van are more neutral.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Heuring3_54-0"><a href="#cite_note-Heuring3-54"><span>[</span>54<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Nolan has said that the film "deals with levels of reality, and perceptions of reality which is something I'm very interested in. It's an action film set in a contemporary world, but with a slight science-fiction bent to it," while also describing it as "very much an ensemble film structured somewhat as a heist movie. It's an action adventure that spans the globe".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-55"><a href="#cite_note-55"><span>[</span>55<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Visual_effects">Visual effects</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=7" title="Edit section: Visual effects">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>For dream sequences in <i>Inception</i>, Nolan used little <a href="/wiki/Computer-generated_imagery" title="Computer-generated imagery">computer-generated imagery</a>, preferring <a href="/wiki/Practical_effect" title="Practical effect">practical effects</a> whenever possible. Nolan said, "It's always very important to me to do as much as possible in-camera, and then, if necessary, computer graphics are very useful to build on or enhance what you have achieved physically."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-InceptionProdNotes6_56-0"><a href="#cite_note-InceptionProdNotes6-56"><span>[</span>56<span>]</span></a></sup> To this end, visual effects supervisor <a href="/wiki/Paul_Franklin_(visual_effects_supervisor)" title="Paul Franklin (visual effects supervisor)">Paul Franklin</a> built a <a href="/wiki/Miniature_effect" title="Miniature effect">miniature</a> of the mountain fortress set and then blew it up for the film. For the fight scene that takes place in zero gravity, he used CG-based effects to "subtly bend elements like physics, space and time."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trussell_57-0"><a href="#cite_note-trussell-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The most challenging effect was the "limbo" city level at the end of the film because it continually developed during production. Franklin had artists build concepts while Nolan gave his ideal vision: "Something glacial, with clear modernist architecture, but with chunks of it breaking off into the sea like icebergs".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trussell_57-1"><a href="#cite_note-trussell-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> Franklin and his team ended up with "something that looked like an iceberg version of <a href="/wiki/Gotham_City" title="Gotham City">Gotham City</a> with water running through it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trussell_57-2"><a href="#cite_note-trussell-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup> They created a basic model of a glacier and then designers created a program that added elements like roads, intersections and ravines until they had a complex, yet organic-looking, cityscape. For the Paris-folding sequence, Franklin had artists producing concept sketches and then they created rough computer animations to give them an idea of what the sequence looked like while in motion. Later during principal photography, Nolan was able to direct Leonardo DiCaprio and Ellen Page based on this rough computer animation Franklin had created. <i>Inception</i> had close to 500 visual effects shots (in comparison, <i><a href="/wiki/Batman_Begins" title="Batman Begins">Batman Begins</a></i> had approximately 620) which is considered minor in comparison to contemporary visual effects epics that can have around 1,500 or 2,000 special effects images.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trussell_57-3"><a href="#cite_note-trussell-57"><span>[</span>57<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Music">Music</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=8" title="Edit section: Music">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Inception_(soundtrack)" title="Inception (soundtrack)">Inception (soundtrack)</a></div>
<p>The score for <i>Inception</i> was written by <a href="/wiki/Hans_Zimmer" title="Hans Zimmer">Hans Zimmer</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-CinemaRewind_26-1"><a href="#cite_note-CinemaRewind-26"><span>[</span>26<span>]</span></a></sup> who described his work as "a very electronic,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-58"><a href="#cite_note-58"><span>[</span>58<span>]</span></a></sup> dense score",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cassidy_59-0"><a href="#cite_note-Cassidy-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> filled with "nostalgia and sadness" to match Cobb's feelings throughout the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martens_60-0"><a href="#cite_note-Martens-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> The music was written simultaneously to filming,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Cassidy_59-1"><a href="#cite_note-Cassidy-59"><span>[</span>59<span>]</span></a></sup> and features a guitar sound reminiscent of <a href="/wiki/Ennio_Morricone" title="Ennio Morricone">Ennio Morricone</a>, played by <a href="/wiki/Johnny_Marr" title="Johnny Marr">Johnny Marr</a>, former guitarist of <a href="/wiki/The_Smiths" title="The Smiths">The Smiths</a>. <a href="/wiki/%C3%89dith_Piaf" title="Édith Piaf">Édith Piaf</a>'s "<a href="/wiki/Non,_je_ne_regrette_rien" title="Non, je ne regrette rien">Non, je ne regrette rien</a>" ("No, I Do Not Regret Anything") pointedly appears throughout the film, used to accurately time the dreams, and Zimmer reworked pieces of the song into cues of the score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Martens_60-1"><a href="#cite_note-Martens-60"><span>[</span>60<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Inception:_Music_from_the_Motion_Picture" title="Inception: Music from the Motion Picture">A soundtrack album</a> was released on July 11, 2010 by <a href="/wiki/Reprise_Records" title="Reprise Records">Reprise Records</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-61"><a href="#cite_note-61"><span>[</span>61<span>]</span></a></sup> The majority of the score was also included in high resolution 5.1 surround sound on the 2nd disc of the 2 disc Blu-ray release <sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-62"><a href="#cite_note-62"><span>[</span>62<span>]</span></a></sup> Hans Zimmer's music was nominated for an Academy Award in the <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Original_Score" title="Academy Award for Best Original Score">Best Original Score</a> category in 2011, losing to <a href="/wiki/Trent_Reznor" title="Trent Reznor">Trent Reznor</a> and <a href="/wiki/Atticus_Ross" title="Atticus Ross">Atticus Ross</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">The Social Network</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscars_63-0"><a href="#cite_note-oscars-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Themes">Themes</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=9" title="Edit section: Themes">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Reality_and_dreams">Reality and dreams</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=10" title="Edit section: Reality and dreams">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Impossible_staircase.svg"><img alt="A staircase in a square format. The stairs make four 90-degree turns in each corner, so they are in the format of a continuous loop." class="thumbimage" data-file-height="283" data-file-width="372" height="167" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Impossible_staircase.svg/220px-Impossible_staircase.svg.png" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Impossible_staircase.svg/330px-Impossible_staircase.svg.png 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/3/34/Impossible_staircase.svg/440px-Impossible_staircase.svg.png 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Impossible_staircase.svg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
<a href="/wiki/Penrose_stairs" title="Penrose stairs">Penrose stairs</a> are incorporated into the film as an example of the <a href="/wiki/Impossible_object" title="Impossible object">impossible objects</a> that can be created in <a href="/wiki/Lucid_dream" title="Lucid dream">lucid dream</a> worlds.</div>
</div>
</div>
<p>In <i>Inception</i>, Nolan wanted to explore "the idea of people sharing a dream space...That gives you the ability to access somebody's <a href="/wiki/Unconscious_mind" title="Unconscious mind">unconscious mind</a>. What would that be used and abused for?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Weintraub_14-6"><a href="#cite_note-Weintraub-14"><span>[</span>14<span>]</span></a></sup> The majority of the film's plot takes place in these interconnected dream worlds. This structure creates a framework where actions in the real or dream worlds ripple across others. The dream is always in a state of production, and shifts across the levels as the characters navigate it.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paul_64-0"><a href="#cite_note-Paul-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> By contrast, the world of <i><a href="/wiki/The_Matrix" title="The Matrix">The Matrix</a></i> (1999) is an authoritarian, computer-controlled one, alluding to theories of social control developed by <a href="/wiki/Michel_Foucault" title="Michel Foucault">Michel Foucault</a> and <a href="/wiki/Jean_Baudrillard" title="Jean Baudrillard">Jean Baudrillard</a>. Nolan's world has more in common with the works of <a href="/wiki/Gilles_Deleuze" title="Gilles Deleuze">Gilles Deleuze</a> and <a href="/wiki/F%C3%A9lix_Guattari" title="Félix Guattari">Félix Guattari</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paul_64-1"><a href="#cite_note-Paul-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Denby_(film_critic)" title="David Denby (film critic)">David Denby</a> in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i> compared Nolan's cinematic treatment of dreams to <a href="/wiki/Luis_Bu%C3%B1uel" title="Luis Buñuel">Luis Buñuel</a>'s in <i><a href="/wiki/Belle_de_Jour_(film)" title="Belle de Jour (film)">Belle de Jour</a></i> (1967) and <i><a href="/wiki/The_Discreet_Charm_of_the_Bourgeoisie" title="The Discreet Charm of the Bourgeoisie">The Discreet Charm of the Bourgeoisie</a></i> (1972).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denby_65-0"><a href="#cite_note-Denby-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> He criticised Nolan's "literal-minded" action level sequencing compared to Buñuel, who "silently pushed us into reveries and left us alone to enjoy our wonderment, but Nolan is working on so many levels of representation at once that he has to lay in pages of dialogue just to explain what's going on." The latter captures "the peculiar malign intensity of actual dreams."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denby_65-1"><a href="#cite_note-Denby-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/Deirdre_Barrett" title="Deirdre Barrett">Deirdre Barrett</a>, a dream researcher at <a href="/wiki/Harvard_University" title="Harvard University">Harvard University</a>, said that Nolan did not get every detail accurate regarding dreams, but their illogical, rambling, disjointed plots would not make for a great thriller anyway. However, "he did get many aspects right," she said, citing the scene in which a sleeping Cobb is shoved into a full bath, and in the dream world water gushes into the windows of the building, waking him up. "That's very much how real stimuli get incorporated, and you very often wake up right after that intrusion".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Breznican_66-0"><a href="#cite_note-Breznican-66"><span>[</span>66<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Nolan himself said, "I tried to work that idea of manipulation and management of a conscious dream being a skill that these people have. Really the script is based on those common, very basic experiences and concepts, and where can those take you? And the only outlandish idea that the film presents, really, is the existence of a technology that allows you to enter and share the same dream as someone else."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Boucher_31-5"><a href="#cite_note-Boucher-31"><span>[</span>31<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Dreams_and_cinema">Dreams and cinema</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=11" title="Edit section: Dreams and cinema">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Others have argued that the film is itself a <a href="/wiki/Oneiric_(film_theory)" title="Oneiric (film theory)">metaphor for film-making</a>, and that the filmgoing experience itself, images flashing before one's eyes in a darkened room, is akin to a dream. Writing in <i>Wired</i>, Jonah Lehrer supported this interpretation and presented neurological evidence that brain activity is strikingly similar during film-watching and sleeping. In both, the <a href="/wiki/Visual_cortex" title="Visual cortex">visual cortex</a> is highly active and the <a href="/wiki/Prefrontal_cortex" title="Prefrontal cortex">prefrontal cortex</a>, which deals with logic, deliberate analysis, and self-awareness, is quiet.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Lehrer_67-0"><a href="#cite_note-Lehrer-67"><span>[</span>67<span>]</span></a></sup> Paul argued that the experience of going to a picturehouse is itself an exercise in shared dreaming, particularly when viewing <i>Inception</i>: the film's sharp cutting between scenes forces the viewer to create larger narrative arcs to stitch the pieces together. This demand of production parallel to consumption of the images, on the part of the audience is analogous to dreaming itself. As in the film's story, in a cinema one enters into the space of another's dream, in this case Nolan's, as with any work of art, one's reading of it is ultimately influenced by one's own subjective desires and subconscious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Paul_64-2"><a href="#cite_note-Paul-64"><span>[</span>64<span>]</span></a></sup> At Bir-Hakeim bridge in Paris, Ariadne creates an illusion of infinity by adding facing mirrors underneath its struts, Stephanie Dreyfus in <i>la Croix</i> asked "Is this not a strong, beautiful metaphor for the cinema and its power of illusion?"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-68"><a href="#cite_note-68"><span>[</span>68<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Cinematic_technique">Cinematic technique</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=12" title="Edit section: Cinematic technique">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Genre">Genre</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=13" title="Edit section: Genre">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="thumb tright">
<div class="thumbinner" style="width:222px;"><a class="image" href="/wiki/File:Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_(without_signature).jpg"><img alt="" class="thumbimage" data-file-height="474" data-file-width="591" height="176" src="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_%28without_signature%29.jpg/220px-Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_%28without_signature%29.jpg" srcset="//upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_%28without_signature%29.jpg/330px-Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_%28without_signature%29.jpg 1.5x, //upload.wikimedia.org/wikipedia/commons/thumb/4/4d/Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_%28without_signature%29.jpg/440px-Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_%28without_signature%29.jpg 2x" width="220"/></a>
<div class="thumbcaption">
<div class="magnify"><a class="internal" href="/wiki/File:Marion_Cotillard_Studio_Harcourt_1999_(without_signature).jpg" title="Enlarge"></a></div>
Marion Cotillard photographed by Studio Harcourt, Paris, in 1999. She plays Mal, a projection of Cobb's subconscious guilt about his beloved wife's suicide. Nolan described the character as "the essence of the <i><a href="/wiki/Femme_fatale" title="Femme fatale">femme fatale</a></i>"–a key trope in <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._9_69-0"><a href="#cite_note-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._9-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup></div>
</div>
</div>
<p>Nolan combined elements from several different film genres into the film, notably science fiction, <a href="/wiki/Heist_film" title="Heist film">heist film</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Film_noir" title="Film noir">film noir</a>. <a href="/wiki/Marion_Cotillard" title="Marion Cotillard">Marion Cotillard</a> plays "Mal" Cobb, Dom Cobb's projection of his guilt over his deceased wife's suicide. As the film's main antagonist, she is a frequent, malevolent presence in his dreams. Dom is unable to control these projections of her, challenging his abilities as an extractor.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-threecircle_15-2"><a href="#cite_note-threecircle-15"><span>[</span>15<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan described Mal as "the essence of the femme fatale",<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._9_69-1"><a href="#cite_note-Production_Notes_2010.2C_p._9-69"><span>[</span>69<span>]</span></a></sup> the key <i>noir</i> reference in the film. As a "classic femme fatale" her relationship with Cobb is in his mind, a manifestation of Cobb's own neurosis and fear of how little he knows about the woman he loves.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired-jan11_70-0"><a href="#cite_note-wired-jan11-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> DiCaprio praised Cotillard's performance saying that "she can be strong and vulnerable and hopeful and heartbreaking all in the same moment, which was perfect for all the contradictions of her character".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-pn10_22-2"><a href="#cite_note-pn10-22"><span>[</span>22<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Nolan began with the structure of a heist movie, since <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Exposition_(literary_technique)" title="Exposition (literary technique)">exposition</a> is an essential element of that genre, though adapted it to have a greater emotional narrative suited to the world of dreams and subconscious.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired-jan11_70-1"><a href="#cite_note-wired-jan11-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> Or, as Denby surmised, "the outer shell of the story is an elaborate caper".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denby_65-2"><a href="#cite_note-Denby-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Thompson" title="Kristin Thompson">Kristin Thompson</a> argued that exposition was a major formal device in the film. While a traditional heist movie has a heavy dose of exposition at the beginning as the team assembles and the leader explains the plan, in <i>Inception</i> this becomes nearly continuous as the group progresses through the various levels of dreaming.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bordwell2_71-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bordwell2-71"><span>[</span>71<span>]</span></a></sup> Three-quarters of the film, until the van begins to fall from the bridge, are devoted to explaining its plot. In this way, exposition takes precedence over characterisation. Their relationships are created by their respective skills and roles. Ariadne, <a href="/wiki/Ariadne" title="Ariadne">like her ancient namesake</a>, creates the maze and guides the others through it, but also helps Cobb navigate his own subconscious, and as the sole student of dream sharing, helps the audience understand the concept of the plot.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Bordwell1_72-0"><a href="#cite_note-Bordwell1-72"><span>[</span>72<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Nolan drew inspiration from the works of <a href="/wiki/Jorge_Luis_Borges" title="Jorge Luis Borges">Jorge Luis Borges</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hiscock_5-7"><a href="#cite_note-Hiscock-5"><span>[</span>5<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-73"><a href="#cite_note-73"><span>[</span>73<span>]</span></a></sup> the <a href="/wiki/Anime" title="Anime">anime</a> film <i><a href="/wiki/Paprika_(2006_film)" title="Paprika (2006 film)">Paprika</a></i> (2006) by the late <a href="/wiki/Satoshi_Kon" title="Satoshi Kon">Satoshi Kon</a> as an influence on the character "Ariadne", and <i><a href="/wiki/Blade_Runner" title="Blade Runner">Blade Runner</a></i> (1982) by <a href="/wiki/Ridley_Scott" title="Ridley Scott">Ridley Scott</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-74"><a href="#cite_note-74"><span>[</span>74<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Ending">Ending</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=14" title="Edit section: Ending">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>The film cuts to the <a href="/wiki/Closing_credits" title="Closing credits">closing credits</a> from a shot of the top beginning to wobble (but not falling), inviting speculation about whether the final sequence was reality or another dream. Nolan confirmed that the ambiguity was deliberate,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-wired-jan11_70-2"><a href="#cite_note-wired-jan11-70"><span>[</span>70<span>]</span></a></sup> saying "I've been asked the question more times than I've ever been asked any other question about any other film I've made... What's funny to me is that people really do expect me to answer it."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insidemovies_75-0"><a href="#cite_note-insidemovies-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> The film's script concludes with "Behind him, on the table, the spinning top is STILL SPINNING. And we – FADE OUT"<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-76"><a href="#cite_note-76"><span>[</span>76<span>]</span></a></sup> Nolan said, "I put that cut there at the end, imposing an ambiguity from outside the film. That always felt the right ending to me – it always felt like the appropriate 'kick' to me... The real point of the scene—and this is what I tell people—is that Cobb isn't looking at the top. He's looking at his kids. He's left it behind. That's the emotional significance of the thing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-insidemovies_75-1"><a href="#cite_note-insidemovies-75"><span>[</span>75<span>]</span></a></sup> Also, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Caine" title="Michael Caine">Michael Caine</a> explained his interpretation of the ending, saying "If I'm there it's real, because I'm never in the dream. I'm the guy who invented the dream."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-77"><a href="#cite_note-77"><span>[</span>77<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Some pundits<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-78"><a href="#cite_note-78"><span>[</span>78<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-79"><a href="#cite_note-79"><span>[</span>79<span>]</span></a></sup> have pointed out that the top was not in fact Cobb's totem, rendering the discussion irrelevant. They point out that the top was Mal's totem; Cobb's was his wedding ring, as he can be seen wearing it whenever he is in a dream and without it whenever he isn't. As he hands his passport to the immigration officer, his hand is shown with no ring; thus he was conclusively in reality when seeing his children. Furthermore, the children were portrayed by different actors,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-80"><a href="#cite_note-80"><span>[</span>80<span>]</span></a></sup> indicating they had aged.</p>
<p>Mark Fisher argued that "a century of cultural theory" cautions against accepting the <a href="/wiki/Authorial_intent" title="Authorial intent">author's interpretation</a> as anything more than a supplementary text, and this all the more so given the theme of the instability of any one master position in Nolan's films. Therein the manipulator is often the one who ends up manipulated and Cobb's "not caring" about whether or not his world is real may be the price of happiness and release.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-81"><a href="#cite_note-81"><span>[</span>81<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Release">Release</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=15" title="Edit section: Release">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Marketing">Marketing</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=16" title="Edit section: Marketing">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>Warner Bros. spent $100 million marketing the film. Although <i>Inception</i> was not part of an existing franchise, Sue Kroll, president of Warner's worldwide marketing, said the company believed it could gain awareness due to the strength of "Christopher Nolan as a brand". Kroll declared that "We don't have the brand equity that usually drives a big summer opening, but we have a great cast and a fresh idea from a filmmaker with a track record of making incredible movies. If you can't make those elements work, it's a sad day."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Fritz2_82-0"><a href="#cite_note-Fritz2-82"><span>[</span>82<span>]</span></a></sup> The studio also tried to maintain a campaign of secrecy—as reported by the Senior VP of Interactive Marketing, Michael Tritter, "You have this movie which is going to have a pretty big built in fanbase... but you also have a movie that you are trying to keep very secret. Chris [Nolan] really likes people to see his movies in a theater and not see it all beforehand so everything that you do to market that—at least early on—is with an eye to feeding the interest to fans."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-83"><a href="#cite_note-83"><span>[</span>83<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>A <a href="/wiki/Viral_marketing" title="Viral marketing">viral marketing</a> campaign was employed for the film. After the revelation of the first teaser trailer, in August 2009, the film's official website featured only an animation of Cobb's spinning top. In December, the top toppled over and the website opened the online game <i>Mind Crime</i>, which upon completion revealed <i>Inception</i> '​s poster.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-84"><a href="#cite_note-84"><span>[</span>84<span>]</span></a></sup> The rest of the campaign unrolled after <a href="/wiki/WonderCon" title="WonderCon">WonderCon</a> in April 2010, where Warner gave away promotional T-shirts featuring the PASIV briefcase used to create the dream space, and had a <a href="/wiki/QR_code" title="QR code">QR code</a> linking to an online manual of the device.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-85"><a href="#cite_note-85"><span>[</span>85<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Mind Crime</i> also received a stage 2 with more resources, including a hidden trailer for the movie.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trailer_86-0"><a href="#cite_note-trailer-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> More pieces of viral marketing began to surface before <i>Inception</i> '​s release, such as a manual filled with bizarre images and text sent to <i><a href="/wiki/Wired_(magazine)" title="Wired (magazine)">Wired</a></i> magazine,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-87"><a href="#cite_note-87"><span>[</span>87<span>]</span></a></sup> and the online publication of posters, ads, phone applications, and strange websites all related to the film.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-88"><a href="#cite_note-88"><span>[</span>88<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-89"><a href="#cite_note-89"><span>[</span>89<span>]</span></a></sup> Warner also released an online prequel comic, <i>Inception: The Cobol Job</i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-90"><a href="#cite_note-90"><span>[</span>90<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The official trailer released on May 10, 2010 through <i>Mind Game</i> was extremely well received.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-trailer_86-1"><a href="#cite_note-trailer-86"><span>[</span>86<span>]</span></a></sup> It featured an original piece of music, "Mind Heist", by recording artist <a href="/wiki/Zack_Hemsey" title="Zack Hemsey">Zack Hemsey</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-91"><a href="#cite_note-91"><span>[</span>91<span>]</span></a></sup> rather than music from the score.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-92"><a href="#cite_note-92"><span>[</span>92<span>]</span></a></sup> The trailer quickly went viral with numerous <a href="/wiki/Mashup_(video)" title="Mashup (video)">mashups</a> copying its style, both by amateurs on sites like YouTube<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-93"><a href="#cite_note-93"><span>[</span>93<span>]</span></a></sup> and by professionals on sites such as <a href="/wiki/CollegeHumor" title="CollegeHumor">CollegeHumor</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-94"><a href="#cite_note-94"><span>[</span>94<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-95"><a href="#cite_note-95"><span>[</span>95<span>]</span></a></sup> On June 7, 2010, a behind-the-scenes featurette on the film was released in HD on Yahoo! Movies.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-96"><a href="#cite_note-96"><span>[</span>96<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Home_media">Home media</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=17" title="Edit section: Home media">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><i>Inception</i> was released on DVD and <a href="/wiki/Blu-ray_Disc" title="Blu-ray Disc">Blu-ray</a> on December 3, 2010, in France,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-97"><a href="#cite_note-97"><span>[</span>97<span>]</span></a></sup> and the week after in the UK and USA (December 7, 2010).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-98"><a href="#cite_note-98"><span>[</span>98<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-99"><a href="#cite_note-99"><span>[</span>99<span>]</span></a></sup> Warner Bros. also made available in the United States a limited Blu-ray edition packaged in a metal replica of the PASIV briefcase, which included extras such as a metal replica of the spinning top totem. With a production run of less than 2000, it sold out in one weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Limited_100-0"><a href="#cite_note-Limited-100"><span>[</span>100<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Putative_video_game">Putative video game<span id="Proposed_video_game"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=18" title="Edit section: Putative video game">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p>In a November 2010 interview, Nolan expressed his intention to develop a video game set in the <i>Inception</i> world, working with a team of collaborators. He described it as "a longer-term proposition", referring to the medium of video games as "something I've wanted to explore".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-101"><a href="#cite_note-101"><span>[</span>101<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Reception">Reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=19" title="Edit section: Reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Box_office_earnings">Box office earnings<span id="Box-office_performance"></span></span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=20" title="Edit section: Box office earnings">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<table class="wikitable" style="width:100%;">
<tr>
<th rowspan="2">Film</th>

<th colspan="3">Box office revenue</th>

<td style="text-align:center;">$532,956,569</td>
<td style="text-align:center;">$825,532,764</td>
