<td style="text-align:center;"><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-102"><a href="#cite_note-102"><span>[</span>102<span>]</span></a></sup></td>
</tr>
</table>
<p><i>Inception</i> was released in both conventional and <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theaters on July 16, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-release_10-1"><a href="#cite_note-release-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-103"><a href="#cite_note-103"><span>[</span>103<span>]</span></a></sup> The film had its world premiere at <a href="/wiki/Leicester_Square" title="Leicester Square">Leicester Square</a> in London, United Kingdom on July 8, 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-104"><a href="#cite_note-104"><span>[</span>104<span>]</span></a></sup> In the United States and Canada, <i>Inception</i> was released theatrically in 3,792 conventional theaters and 195 <a href="/wiki/IMAX" title="IMAX">IMAX</a> theaters.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-release_10-2"><a href="#cite_note-release-10"><span>[</span>10<span>]</span></a></sup> The film grossed $21.8 million during its opening day on July 16, 2010, with midnight screenings in 1,500 locations.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-105"><a href="#cite_note-105"><span>[</span>105<span>]</span></a></sup> Overall the film made $62.7 million and debuted at No.1 on its opening weekend.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo-weekend_106-0"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-weekend-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Inception</i> '​s opening weekend gross made it the second-highest-grossing debut for a <a href="/wiki/Science_fiction_film" title="Science fiction film">science-fiction film</a> that was not a sequel, remake or adaptation, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Avatar_(2009_film)" title="Avatar (2009 film)">Avatar</a></i> '​s $77 million opening weekend gross in 2009.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-mojo-weekend_106-1"><a href="#cite_note-mojo-weekend-106"><span>[</span>106<span>]</span></a></sup> The film held the top spot of the box office rankings in its second and third weekends, with drops of just 32% ($42.7 million) and 36% ($27.5 million) respectively,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-107"><a href="#cite_note-107"><span>[</span>107<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-108"><a href="#cite_note-108"><span>[</span>108<span>]</span></a></sup> before dropping to second place in its fourth week, behind <i><a href="/wiki/The_Other_Guys" title="The Other Guys">The Other Guys</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-109"><a href="#cite_note-109"><span>[</span>109<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i>Inception</i> grossed US$292 million in the United States and Canada, US$56 million in the United Kingdom, Ireland and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> and US$475 million in other countries for a total of $823 million.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Mojo_3-3"><a href="#cite_note-Mojo-3"><span>[</span>3<span>]</span></a></sup> Its five highest-grossing markets after the USA and Canada (US$292) were China (US$68million), the United Kingdom, Ireland and <a href="/wiki/Malta" title="Malta">Malta</a> (US$56 million), France and the <a href="/wiki/Maghreb" title="Maghreb">Maghreb</a> region (US$43 million), Japan (US$40 million) and <a href="/wiki/South_Korea" title="South Korea">South Korea</a> (US$38 million).<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-110"><a href="#cite_note-110"><span>[</span>110<span>]</span></a></sup> It was the sixth-highest grossing film of 2010 in North America,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-111"><a href="#cite_note-111"><span>[</span>111<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/2010_in_film#Highest-grossing_films" title="2010 in film">fourth-highest internationally</a>, behind <i><a href="/wiki/Toy_Story_3" title="Toy Story 3">Toy Story 3</a></i>, <i><a href="/wiki/Alice_in_Wonderland_(2010_film)" title="Alice in Wonderland (2010 film)">Alice in Wonderland</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Harry_Potter_and_the_Deathly_Hallows_-_Part_1" title="Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows - Part 1">Harry Potter and the Deathly Hallows - Part 1</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-112"><a href="#cite_note-112"><span>[</span>112<span>]</span></a></sup> The film currently stands as the <a href="/wiki/List_of_highest-grossing_films" title="List of highest-grossing films">42nd-highest-grossing of all time</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-113"><a href="#cite_note-113"><span>[</span>113<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Inception</i> is the third most lucrative production in <a href="/wiki/Christopher_Nolan" title="Christopher Nolan">Christopher Nolan</a>'s career—behind <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_(film)" title="The Dark Knight (film)">The Dark Knight</a></i> and <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/The_Dark_Knight_Rises_(film)" title="The Dark Knight Rises (film)">The Dark Knight Rises</a></i><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-114"><a href="#cite_note-114"><span>[</span>114<span>]</span></a></sup>— and the second most for <a href="/wiki/Leonardo_DiCaprio" title="Leonardo DiCaprio">Leonardo DiCaprio</a>—behind <i><a href="/wiki/Titanic_(1997_film)" title="Titanic (1997 film)">Titanic</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-115"><a href="#cite_note-115"><span>[</span>115<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Critical_reception">Critical reception</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=21" title="Edit section: Critical reception">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<p><span id="Critics"></span> <a href="/wiki/Rotten_Tomatoes" title="Rotten Tomatoes">Rotten Tomatoes</a> gave the film a score of 86% based on reviews from 284 critics, with an average score of 8/10. The website reported the critical consensus as "smart, innovative, and thrilling, <i>Inception</i> is that rare summer blockbuster that succeeds viscerally as well as intellectually."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-tomatoes_116-0"><a href="#cite_note-tomatoes-116"><span>[</span>116<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Metacritic" title="Metacritic">Metacritic</a>, another review aggregator, assigned the film a weighted average score of 74 (out of 100) based on 42 reviews from mainstream critics, considered to be "generally favorable reviews."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-metacritic_117-0"><a href="#cite_note-metacritic-117"><span>[</span>117<span>]</span></a></sup> In polls conducted by <a href="/wiki/CinemaScore" title="CinemaScore">CinemaScore</a> during the opening weekend cinemagoers gave <i>Inception</i> an average score of "B+".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-118"><a href="#cite_note-118"><span>[</span>118<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>While some critics have tended to view the film as perfectly straightforward, and even criticize its overarching themes as "the stuff of torpid platitudes," online discussion has been much more positive.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-119"><a href="#cite_note-119"><span>[</span>119<span>]</span></a></sup> Heated debate has centered on the ambiguity of the ending, with many critics like Devin Faraci making the case that the film is self-referential and tongue-in-cheek, both a film about film-making and a dream about dreams.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-120"><a href="#cite_note-120"><span>[</span>120<span>]</span></a></sup> Other critics read <i>Inception</i> as Christian allegory and focus on the film's use of religious and water symbolism.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-121"><a href="#cite_note-121"><span>[</span>121<span>]</span></a></sup> Yet other critics, such as <a href="/wiki/Kristin_Thompson" title="Kristin Thompson">Kristin Thompson</a>, see less value in the ambiguous ending of the film and more in its structure and novel method of storytelling, highlighting <i>Inception</i> as a new form of narrative that revels in "continuous exposition".<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-122"><a href="#cite_note-122"><span>[</span>122<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Whatever its meaning, the film has had excellent reviews in general. Perhaps playing off the film's game imagery, <i><a href="/wiki/Rolling_Stone" title="Rolling Stone">Rolling Stone</a></i> magazine's <a href="/wiki/Peter_Travers" title="Peter Travers">Peter Travers</a> called <i>Inception</i> a "wildly ingenious chess game," and concluded "the result is a knockout."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-123"><a href="#cite_note-123"><span>[</span>123<span>]</span></a></sup> In <i><a href="/wiki/Variety_(magazine)" title="Variety (magazine)">Variety</a></i>, Justin Chang praised the film as "a conceptual <a class="extiw" href="//en.wiktionary.org/wiki/tour_de_force" title="wiktionary:tour de force">tour de force</a>" and wrote, "applying a vivid sense of procedural detail to a fiendishly intricate yarn set in the <a href="/wiki/Labyrinth" title="Labyrinth">labyrinth</a> of the <a href="/wiki/Unconscious_mind" title="Unconscious mind">unconscious mind</a>, the writer-director has devised a heist thriller for <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Surrealist" title="Surrealist">surrealists</a>, a <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Jung" title="Jung">Jungian</a>'s <i><a href="/wiki/Rififi" title="Rififi">Rififi</a></i>, that challenges viewers to sift through multiple layers of (un)reality."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-variety-review_124-0"><a href="#cite_note-variety-review-124"><span>[</span>124<span>]</span></a></sup> Jim Vejvoda of <a href="/wiki/IGN" title="IGN">IGN</a> rated the film as perfect, deeming it "a singular accomplishment from a filmmaker who has only gotten better with each film."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-125"><a href="#cite_note-125"><span>[</span>125<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Relevant_Magazine" title="Relevant Magazine">Relevant Magazine</a></i> '​s David Roark called it Nolan's greatest accomplishment, saying, "Visually, intellectually and emotionally, <i>Inception</i> is a masterpiece."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-126"><a href="#cite_note-126"><span>[</span>126<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><i><a href="/wiki/Empire_(film_magazine)" title="Empire (film magazine)">Empire</a></i> magazine rated it five stars in the August 2010 issue and wrote, "it feels like <a href="/wiki/Stanley_Kubrick" title="Stanley Kubrick">Stanley Kubrick</a> adapting the work of the great sci-fi author <a href="/wiki/William_Gibson" title="William Gibson">William Gibson</a> ... Nolan delivers another true original: welcome to an undiscovered country."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-127"><a href="#cite_note-127"><span>[</span>127<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Entertainment_Weekly" title="Entertainment Weekly">Entertainment Weekly</a></i> gave the film a B+ rating and Lisa Schwarzbaum wrote, "It's a rolling explosion of images as hypnotizing and sharply angled as any in a drawing by <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/M.C._Escher" title="M.C. Escher">M.C. Escher</a> or a state-of-the-biz videogame; the backwards splicing of Nolan's own <i>Memento</i> looks rudimentary by comparison."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-128"><a href="#cite_note-128"><span>[</span>128<span>]</span></a></sup> The <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_Post" title="New York Post">New York Post</a></i> gave the film a four-star rating and <a href="/wiki/Lou_Lumenick" title="Lou Lumenick">Lou Lumenick</a> wrote, "DiCaprio, who has never been better as the tortured hero, draws you in with a love story that will appeal even to non-sci-fi fans."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-129"><a href="#cite_note-129"><span>[</span>129<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Roger_Ebert" title="Roger Ebert">Roger Ebert</a> of the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Sun-Times" title="Chicago Sun-Times">Chicago Sun-Times</a></i> awarded the film a full four stars and said that <i>Inception</i> "is all about process, about fighting our way through enveloping sheets of reality and dream, reality within dreams, dreams without reality. It's a breathtaking juggling act."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-130"><a href="#cite_note-130"><span>[</span>130<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Richard_Roeper" title="Richard Roeper">Richard Roeper</a>, also of the <i>Sun-Times</i>, gave <i>Inception</i> a perfect score of "A+" and called it "one of the best movies of the [21st] century."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-131"><a href="#cite_note-131"><span>[</span>131<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p><a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_5_Live" title="BBC Radio 5 Live">BBC Radio 5 Live</a>'s <a href="/wiki/Mark_Kermode" title="Mark Kermode">Mark Kermode</a> named <i>Inception</i> as the best film of 2010, stating "Inception is proof that people are not stupid, that cinema is not trash, and that it is possible for blockbusters and art to be the same thing."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Kermode_132-0"><a href="#cite_note-Kermode-132"><span>[</span>132<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In his review for the <i><a href="/wiki/Chicago_Tribune" title="Chicago Tribune">Chicago Tribune</a></i>, <a href="/wiki/Michael_Phillips_(critic)" title="Michael Phillips (critic)">Michael Phillips</a> gave the film 3 stars out of 4 and wrote, "I found myself wishing <i>Inception</i> were weirder, further out ... the film is Nolan's labyrinth all the way, and it's gratifying to experience a summer movie with large visual ambitions and with nothing more or less on its mind than (as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Shakespeare" title="Shakespeare">Shakespeare</a> said) a dream that hath no bottom."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-133"><a href="#cite_note-133"><span>[</span>133<span>]</span></a></sup> <i>Time</i> magazine's <a href="/wiki/Richard_Corliss" title="Richard Corliss">Richard Corliss</a> wrote the film's "noble intent is to implant one man's vision in the mind of a vast audience ... The idea of moviegoing as communal dreaming is a century old. With <i>Inception</i>, viewers have a chance to see that notion get a state-of-the-art update."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-134"><a href="#cite_note-134"><span>[</span>134<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> '​ <a href="/wiki/Kenneth_Turan" title="Kenneth Turan">Kenneth Turan</a> felt that Nolan was able to blend "the best of traditional and modern filmmaking. If you're searching for smart and nervy popular entertainment, this is what it looks like."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-135"><a href="#cite_note-135"><span>[</span>135<span>]</span></a></sup> <i><a href="/wiki/USA_Today" title="USA Today">USA Today</a></i> rated the film three-and-a-half stars out of four and Claudia Puig felt that Nolan "regards his viewers as possibly smarter than they are—or at least as capable of rising to his inventive level. That's a tall order. But it's refreshing to find a director who makes us stretch, even occasionally struggle, to keep up."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-136"><a href="#cite_note-136"><span>[</span>136<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Not all reviewers gave the film positive reviews. <i><a href="/wiki/New_York_(magazine)" title="New York (magazine)">New York</a></i> magazine's <a href="/wiki/David_Edelstein" title="David Edelstein">David Edelstein</a> claimed in his review to "have no idea what so many people are raving about. It's as if someone went into their heads while they were sleeping and planted the idea that <i>Inception</i> is a visionary masterpiece and—hold on ... Whoa! I think I get it. The movie is a metaphor for the power of delusional hype—a metaphor for itself."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-137"><a href="#cite_note-137"><span>[</span>137<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/Rex_Reed" title="Rex Reed">Rex Reed</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Observer" title="The New York Observer">The New York Observer</a></i> explained the film's development as "pretty much what we've come to expect from summer movies in general and Christopher Nolan movies in particular ... [it] doesn't seem like much of an accomplishment to me."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-138"><a href="#cite_note-138"><span>[</span>138<span>]</span></a></sup> <a href="/wiki/A._O._Scott" title="A. O. Scott">A. O. Scott</a> of <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_York_Times" title="The New York Times">The New York Times</a></i> commented "there is a lot to see in <i>Inception</i>, there is nothing that counts as genuine vision. Mr. Nolan's idea of the mind is too literal, too logical, and too rule-bound to allow the full measure of madness."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-139"><a href="#cite_note-139"><span>[</span>139<span>]</span></a></sup> <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/David_Denby_(film_critic)" title="David Denby (film critic)">David Denby</a>, writing in <i><a href="/wiki/The_New_Yorker" title="The New Yorker">The New Yorker</a></i>, considered the film not nearly as much fun as Nolan imagined it to be, concluding "<i>Inception</i> is a stunning-looking film that gets lost in fabulous intricacies, a movie devoted to its own workings and to little else."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Denby_65-3"><a href="#cite_note-Denby-65"><span>[</span>65<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>Several sources have noted many plot similarities between the film and the 2002 <a href="/wiki/Scrooge_McDuck" title="Scrooge McDuck">Uncle Scrooge</a> comic <i><a href="/wiki/The_Dream_of_a_Lifetime" title="The Dream of a Lifetime">The Dream of a Lifetime</a></i> by <a href="/wiki/Don_Rosa" title="Don Rosa">Don Rosa</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-140"><a href="#cite_note-140"><span>[</span>140<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-141"><a href="#cite_note-141"><span>[</span>141<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-142"><a href="#cite_note-142"><span>[</span>142<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In April 2014, <i><a href="/wiki/The_Daily_Telegraph" title="The Daily Telegraph">The Daily Telegraph</a></i> placed the title on their top ten list of the most overrated films. <i>Telegraph</i> '​s Tim Robey stated "It's a criminal failing of the movie that it purports to be about people’s dreams being invaded, but demonstrates no instinct at all for what a dream has ever felt like, and no flair for making us feel like we're in one, at any point."<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-143"><a href="#cite_note-143"><span>[</span>143<span>]</span></a></sup> The film won an informal poll by The <i><a href="/wiki/Los_Angeles_Times" title="Los Angeles Times">Los Angeles Times</a></i> as the most overrated movie of 2010.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-144"><a href="#cite_note-144"><span>[</span>144<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>In March 2011, the film was voted by <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1" title="BBC Radio 1">BBC Radio 1</a> and <a href="/wiki/BBC_Radio_1Xtra" title="BBC Radio 1Xtra">BBC Radio 1Xtra</a> listeners as their ninth favorite film of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-145"><a href="#cite_note-145"><span>[</span>145<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2012, <i>Inception</i> was ranked the 35th Best Edited Film of All Time by the <a href="/wiki/Motion_Picture_Editors_Guild" title="Motion Picture Editors Guild">Motion Picture Editors Guild</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-editorsguild_146-0"><a href="#cite_note-editorsguild-146"><span>[</span>146<span>]</span></a></sup> In the same year, <a href="/wiki/Total_Film" title="Total Film">Total Film</a> named it the most rewatchable movie of all time.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Rewatchable_147-0"><a href="#cite_note-Rewatchable-147"><span>[</span>147<span>]</span></a></sup> In 2014, <i>Empire</i> ranked <i>Inception</i> the tenth greatest film ever made on their list of "The 301 Greatest Movies Of All Time" as voted by the magazine's readers,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-148"><a href="#cite_note-148"><span>[</span>148<span>]</span></a></sup> while <i>Rolling Stone</i> magazine named it the second best science fiction film since the turn of the century.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-149"><a href="#cite_note-149"><span>[</span>149<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h3><span class="mw-headline" id="Accolades">Accolades</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=22" title="Edit section: Accolades">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h3>
<div class="hatnote relarticle mainarticle">Main article: <a href="/wiki/List_of_accolades_received_by_Inception" title="List of accolades received by Inception">List of accolades received by Inception</a></div>
<p><i>Inception</i> appeared on over 273 critics' lists of the top ten films of 2010, being picked as No.1 on 55 of those lists. It was the second most mentioned film in both the top ten and No.1 lists only behind <i><a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">The Social Network</a></i> and was one of the most critically acclaimed films of 2010, alongside the former, <i><a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_Speech" title="The King's Speech">The King's Speech</a></i>, and <i><a href="/wiki/Black_Swan_(film)" title="Black Swan (film)">Black Swan</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-150"><a href="#cite_note-150"><span>[</span>150<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<p>The film won many awards in technical categories, such as <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Academy_Award" title="Academy Award">Academy Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Cinematography" title="Academy Award for Best Cinematography">Best Cinematography</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound_Editing" title="Academy Award for Best Sound Editing">Best Sound Editing</a>, <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Sound" title="Academy Award for Best Sound">Best Sound Mixing</a>, and <a href="/wiki/Academy_Award_for_Best_Visual_Effects" title="Academy Award for Best Visual Effects">Best Visual Effects</a>,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscars_63-1"><a href="#cite_note-oscars-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup> and the <a href="/wiki/British_Academy_Film_Awards" title="British Academy Film Awards">British Academy Film Awards</a> for <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Production_Design" title="BAFTA Award for Best Production Design">Best Production Design</a>, <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Special_Visual_Effects" title="BAFTA Award for Best Special Visual Effects">Best Special Visual Effects</a> and <a href="/wiki/BAFTA_Award_for_Best_Sound" title="BAFTA Award for Best Sound">Best Sound</a>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAFTA_151-0"><a href="#cite_note-BAFTA-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup> In most of its artistic nominations, such as Film, Director, and Screenplay at the Oscars, BAFTAs and <a class="mw-redirect" href="/wiki/Golden_Globe_Awards" title="Golden Globe Awards">Golden Globes</a>, the film was defeated by <i><a href="/wiki/The_Social_Network" title="The Social Network">The Social Network</a></i> and <i><a href="/wiki/The_King%27s_Speech" title="The King's Speech">The King's Speech</a></i>.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-oscars_63-2"><a href="#cite_note-oscars-63"><span>[</span>63<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-BAFTA_151-1"><a href="#cite_note-BAFTA-151"><span>[</span>151<span>]</span></a></sup><sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-152"><a href="#cite_note-152"><span>[</span>152<span>]</span></a></sup> However, the film did win the two highest honors for a science fiction or fantasy film: the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Bradbury_Award" title="Bradbury Award">Bradbury Award</a> for best dramatic production<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Nebulas_153-0"><a href="#cite_note-Nebulas-153"><span>[</span>153<span>]</span></a></sup> and the 2011 <a href="/wiki/Hugo_Award" title="Hugo Award">Hugo Award</a> for best dramatic presentation, long form.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-Hugos_154-0"><a href="#cite_note-Hugos-154"><span>[</span>154<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="Possible_sequels">Possible sequels</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=23" title="Edit section: Possible sequels">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p>When asked if there will be a sequel, Nolan responded “It’s not something I want to say no to, but it’s not something I’ve given a lot of thought about.”<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-155"><a href="#cite_note-155"><span>[</span>155<span>]</span></a></sup> Tom Hardy said he and the rest of the cast had signed on for possible sequels, but is unsure if there will be any.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-156"><a href="#cite_note-156"><span>[</span>156<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="In_popular_culture">In popular culture</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=24" title="Edit section: In popular culture">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>
<p><a href="/wiki/Asaf_Avidan" title="Asaf Avidan">Asaf Avidan</a>'s "The Labyrinth Song", from his album "<a href="/wiki/Gold_Shadow" title="Gold Shadow">Gold Shadow</a>" is set in the film and speaks from one of the character's perspectives. Numerous pop and hip-hop songs reference Inception,<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-157"><a href="#cite_note-157"><span>[</span>157<span>]</span></a></sup> including Common (Blue Sky), N.E.R.D. (Hypnotize U), XV (The Kick), The Black Eyed Peas (Just Can’t Get Enough), Lil Wayne (6 Foot 7 Foot feat. Cory Gunz), J. Lo (On The Floor feat. Pitbull), and B.O.B. (Strange Clouds), while TI had Inception-based artwork in two of his mixtapes. An instrumental track by Joe Budden is titled Inception.</p>
<p>Numerous television shows have also made reference to or have parodied Inception.<sup class="reference" id="cite_ref-158"><a href="#cite_note-158"><span>[</span>158<span>]</span></a></sup></p>
<h2><span class="mw-headline" id="See_also">See also</span><span class="mw-editsection"><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">[</span><a href="/w/index.php?title=Inception&amp;action=edit&amp;section=25" title="Edit section: See also">edit</a><span class="mw-editsection-bracket">]</span></span></h2>

<tr>
<th class="navbox-group" scope="row">Nebula Award for Best Script</th>
<td class="navbox-list navbox-odd hlist" style="text-align:left;border-left-width:2px;border-left-style:solid;width:100%;padding:0px">
<div style="padding:0em 0.25em">
<ul>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Soylent_Green" title="Soylent Green">Soylent Green</a></i> – Stanley R. Greenberg (1973)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Sleeper_(1973_film)" title="Sleeper (1973 film)">Sleeper</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/Woody_Allen" title="Woody Allen">Woody Allen</a> (1974)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Young_Frankenstein" title="Young Frankenstein">Young Frankenstein</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/Mel_Brooks" title="Mel Brooks">Mel Brooks</a> and <a href="/wiki/Gene_Wilder" title="Gene Wilder">Gene Wilder</a> (1975)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Star_Wars_(film)" title="Star Wars (film)">Star Wars</a></i> (1977)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/The_Sixth_Sense" title="The Sixth Sense">The Sixth Sense</a></i> – <a href="/wiki/M._Night_Shyamalan" title="M. Night Shyamalan">M. Night Shyamalan</a> (1999)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Galaxy_Quest" title="Galaxy Quest">Galaxy Quest</a></i> – David Howard &amp; <a href="/wiki/Robert_Gordon_(screenwriter)" title="Robert Gordon (screenwriter)">Robert Gordon</a> (2000)</li>
<li><i><a href="/wiki/Crouching_Tiger,_Hidden_Dragon" title="Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon">Crouching Tiger, Hidden Dragon</a></i> <a href="/wiki/James_Schamus" title="James Schamus">James Schamus</a>, Kuo Jung Tsai and Hui-Ling Wang (2001)</li>
